  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bc302034-3984-40d7-ad19-e7a55886b395'

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I don't know if this is accurate, but this is purely my interpertation.. IMy thoughts were that he was actually a she, because at the end of the story<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I don't know if this is accurate, but this is purely my interpertation.. IMy thoughts were that he was actually a she, because at the end of the story she said, "he was no man". My theory is that she actually went crazy and killed her sisters, bc in the pics, as she was looking for sisters in the house you could see the "man" hidden in several different places . Meaning, to me, that the person who killed her sisters and her sisters bodies was still in the house. I'm not really sure. It's just a theory I have and I have pondered this story for a while. I will say out of all the stories in the book, I found this one to be the most disturbing. Mainly because it remains a mystery to me. If anyoe finds out the real interpertation, please que me in! <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I work in an elementary school library and we are making this a young adult book for our grades 6-8. While it is freaky, there isn't any thing inappro<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I work in an elementary school library and we are making this a young adult book for our grades 6-8. While it is freaky, there isn't any thing inappropriate language, sexual, etc wise. There is some murder, a story about finding body parts, and some pictures dictating smeared blood but for those who enjoy horror, the stories are mysterious and intriguing so the pictures add great excitement to the read. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_4').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

  <span id="freeText80936914712891268" style="display:none">This book freaked my shit out.<br /><br />Yeah. How's that for a blurb? <br /><br />"This freaked my shit out." <br /> - Patrick Rothfuss<br /><br />The truth is, this book is amazing. I've read a lot of great comics this last year, and out of all of them, this is the one that had the most profound emotional effect on me. <br /><br />It's not gory, or graphic. It's... unsettling. It's creepy. It's like the darkest of the old-school faerie tales.<br /><br />I read it at night before I was going to go to bed. And when I was done, I was too unnerved to go to sleep. I had to read something else to settle myself down first. <br /><br />Seriously. I'm 40 years old. And still this thing got to me. <br /><br /><br />Highly *highly* recommended.</span>

<div id="review_1159232110" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1159232110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11296890452836655166"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420615182i/13245485._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='260' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Goosebumps. Full of them. Reading this <i>horror filled</i> graphic novel during night-time turned out to be a terrifying idea. Yet, I couldn’t stop reading. It was captivating. I don’t think I’ve even noted a single thing of my environment while reading it; there was only the book and I. <br/><br/>There were five short stories in this book. All of them contained a spooky or completely frightening plot that will keep you on the edge. The author also managed to include suspense in the atmosphere. However scary th</span>
  <span id="freeText11296890452836655166" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420615182i/13245485._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Goosebumps. Full of them. Reading this <i>horror filled</i> graphic novel during night-time turned out to be a terrifying idea. Yet, I couldn’t stop reading. It was captivating. I don’t think I’ve even noted a single thing of my environment while reading it; there was only the book and I. <br><br>There were five short stories in this book. All of them contained a spooky or completely frightening plot that will keep you on the edge. The author also managed to include suspense in the atmosphere. However scary the story or characters might have appeared, there was no possibility for me to interrupt my own reading. The stories were short which means that never was I bored or waiting for something interesting to happen. It’s not often that I take the time to read and admire graphic novels and there are multiple styles of drawings that I am still not used to, but this is one I found uniquely beautiful and would gladly see more of.<br><br>The writing was simplistic but, sincerely, it worked with every single thing. Plus, it is really on the illustrations – which were amazingly vivid and arresting too – that I was concentrated on and did not, as I usually do, have the reflex to observe and wonder if the author used repetition as well as some figures of speech from time to time.<br><br>My own personal favorite was ‘A Lady’s Hands Are Cold’ since, at first, I thought it to be a retelling of ‘Bluebeard’ and was curious to see which path the story and main character will take. Plus, the author noticeably surpassed herself with the graphics in that short story in question.<br><br>It is true that I found this graphic novel to be one of the best I have ever read, for how monopolized by it I was the whole reading time, but there is something that displeased me inside it: <b>every short story ended on a cliffhanger.</b> Now, that was frustrating. At first, I thought maybe I was missing something but then it happened again. And again. Every time. Maybe some will not mind it, but by how dark the endings were, I did not approve of the hypotheses my mind was making for the characters.<br><br>This is one graphic novel I highly recommend to every fan of dark fairy tales and graphic novels with eerie ambiences. A truly too short for my liking book, but impressive nonetheless.<br><br>PS. How am I ever going to be able to sleep tonight? I have to get my head off worms, wolves, ghosts, hair-raising monsters hiding under the bed…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420615182i/13245486._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420615182i/13245487._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11296890452836655166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</a><br/><br/>if i were judging this book solely on its artwork, it would be an easy five stars. there are five main stories, plus an introduction and a conclusion, each with their own style of illustration. it's not that i love them all equally, but i do generally appreciate range and variety :<br/><br/><a href='http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6522_zpsol64vjex.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/><a href='http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6517_zpsxvhzpiys.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a> <br/><br/><a href='http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6492_zpsx6b0m0d3.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>in a way, it kind of reminded me of <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=buoG3gLa6Ik' rel='nofollow noopener'>fear(s) of the dark</a>, a film in which several different illustrators bring their own brand of creepy to life through unique animation stylings: <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015949._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015950.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015951._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015952._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015953.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>this book is obvio</span>
  <span id="freeText14241694868832932769" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6490_zpsbefalcqk.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928835._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6490_zpsbefalcqk.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>if i were judging this book solely on its artwork, it would be an easy five stars. there are five main stories, plus an introduction and a conclusion, each with their own style of illustration. it's not that i love them all equally, but i do generally appreciate range and variety :<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6522_zpsol64vjex.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928818._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6522_zpsol64vjex.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6517_zpsxvhzpiys.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928822._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6517_zpsxvhzpiys.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6503_zpswrjag6ij.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928831._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6503_zpswrjag6ij.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6492_zpsx6b0m0d3.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928834._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6492_zpsx6b0m0d3.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>in a way, it kind of reminded me of <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=buoG3gLa6Ik" rel="nofollow noopener">fear(s) of the dark</a>, a film in which several different illustrators bring their own brand of creepy to life through unique animation stylings: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015949._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015950.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015951._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015952._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454799212i/18015953.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>this book is obviously more limited in its range because it is all coming from a single imagination, but as far as artwork goes, i dig it<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6499_zpskiqtupv2.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928832._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6499_zpskiqtupv2.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>however, the stories were mostly just okay. <br><br>they are definitely not scary, or weren't to me anyway, and they fall more on the side of "atmospheric" or "ominous" than "you will never sleep again."<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6518_zpsqwzktp0z.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928824._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6518_zpsqwzktp0z.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>which, considering this is meant as a YA book is probably for the best, but i'm still looking for my big scare, and i fear it will never come. <br><br>which is totally the wrong kind of fear.<br><br><b>an introduction</b><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6493_zpsyqlxb8jj.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928836._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6493_zpsyqlxb8jj.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>this is just a little tease, not so much a story as a setting of the mood for what is to come. <br><br><b>our neighbor's house</b><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6496_zpsv9p6ldst.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928833._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6496_zpsv9p6ldst.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>this one feels very familiar. there's an olde timey new england vibe to it, and while i don't think it's actually <i>based</i> on anything, it feels like a mashup of a bunch of different stories, like something that would be read aloud in a spoooooky voice during a haunted hayride right before costumed people come running out of the woods all clawing and moaning to the delighted shrieks of girl scouts. makes me want to drink warm cider. <br><br><b>a lady's hands are cold</b><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6510_zpspbojenox.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928830._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6510_zpspbojenox.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>this had probably my favorite artwork of the bunch<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6509_zpsj81j5htt.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928829._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6509_zpsj81j5htt.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and i enjoyed the way it exploded offa the page<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6508_zpsennen3iv.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928828._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6508_zpsennen3iv.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and it's also in the running for top story (along with <i>our neighbor's house</i>). this one reads more like a fairy tale than the others; a little hint of bluebeard but with fewer wives, more property damage, and much less gratitude.<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6504_zpsvdaxh0ko.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456006558i/18179576._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6504_zpsvdaxh0ko.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>his face all red</b><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6513_zpswlrq4tju.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928827._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6513_zpswlrq4tju.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>i'm honestly not sure what happened in this one. maybe i'm missing some subtlety, but near as i can figure, this is the story arc:<br><br>-spooky tease/declaration<br>-backtrack<br>-story story story<br>-action!<br>-repercussions of action<br>-spooky happenings<br>-investigation<br>-confirmation that previous action! occurred<br>-the end<br><br>i don't understand this at all. there's an expectation of some kind of twist or reveal, but instead the ending is like someone going through the house on their way to bed: yup, door's locked, stove's off, cat has water, everything is where i thought it was...<br><br>what am i missing? <br><br><b>my friend janna</b><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6516_zpsa8g6jwfm.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928826._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6516_zpsa8g6jwfm.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>this has the bones of a very traditional ghost story, but there's just too <i>much</i> story around what could have been a genuinely spooky read if it didn't meander so much. i think horror works best when it is streamlined, when there's ambiguity left over for the reader to fill in with their own worst imaginings and also when the journey is straight and fast and decisive like a gunshot or a thunderclap. this one is so frontloaded with unfocused exposition at the beginning that you get lulled into what is ultimately a very gentle horror. i think the illustrations work particularly well in conjunction with this story, but i also think it would have been much more effective if it were whittled down a bit.<br><br><b>the nesting place</b><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6520_zpsnkgytcbp.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928820._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6520_zpsnkgytcbp.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>another one - no idea, really, what's going on here. i mean, i understand the basic plot, but it's the details that leave me head-scratching. the prologue seems to suggest that the ... situation is location-specific, but that's clearly not the case, nor is it familial, although it tangentially affects a family over generations, and i know what i JUST SAID about ambiguity being good for horror, but how does that ending work? is it both? or migrated? and aren't they going to the very same city that was effective as a threat and avoided on the previous page? i don't understaaaaaand! <br><br><b>in conclusion</b><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/flat%20stanley/IMG_6524_zps7y7rxra2.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454183727i/17928816._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_6524_zps7y7rxra2.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>this is another little shorty - the urban legend rim shot to end end the collection on a pop. it's a little red riding hood offshoot whose zinger is pretty much the same shape as this joke that i am spoiler tagging for people who don't think pedophile jokes are ever funny:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A pedophile walks through the woods with a child. The child says, "These woods are scary." The pedophile says, "Tell me about it. I have to walk back through here alone." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>different punch line, but the same basic "gotcha!" energy. <br><br>i'm giving it a four because i did like the artwork, but the stories themselves are pretty patchy, so i'm being a bit generous here. <br><br>dear books - please be scarier for me!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14241694868832932769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</a><br/><br/>I didn't.<br/>I think I may not be the target audience for something like this. <br/>I'm not really a fan of short stories. At least the ones that have no definite endings. <br/><a href='http://s926.photobucket.com/user/bookqueenshelby/media/through-the-woods-teaser_zpspuoptnnc.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>It does have some awesome artwork though. I think if I had read these when I was a teenager I went have went bonkers over them. But my old jaded ass just didn't care for it now bec</span>
  <span id="freeText14956706932985075883" style="display:none">A set of five short little horror stories. <br>Everyone loves this book.<br>Everyone says don't read these at dark.<br>I thought I would flip out over this book.<br><a href="http://s926.photobucket.com/user/bookqueenshelby/media/through-the-woods-red-riding-hood_zpscxh06z0a.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442341153i/16220518._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo through-the-woods-red-riding-hood_zpscxh06z0a.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I didn't.<br>I think I may not be the target audience for something like this. <br>I'm not really a fan of short stories. At least the ones that have no definite endings. <br><a href="http://s926.photobucket.com/user/bookqueenshelby/media/through-the-woods-teaser_zpspuoptnnc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442341153i/16220519._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo through-the-woods-teaser_zpspuoptnnc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It does have some awesome artwork though. I think if I had read these when I was a teenager I went have went bonkers over them. But my old jaded ass just didn't care for it now because it takes more than spaghetti head to scare me now.<br><a href="http://s926.photobucket.com/user/bookqueenshelby/media/5_creepy_comics_header_alt_zpscu47tut7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

I have no clue why he is not at the top of that game because he is one of the best at it that I've seen. </span>

<div id="review_1184720635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1184720635" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1184720635?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-women">gn-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-short-stories">gn-short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-horror">gn-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-ya">gn-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1184720635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer866138568399863905">11/11/18: I reread this book because I reviewed and shared some of her free short stories here for Halloween, and because I read Speak: The Graphic Novel, which she illustrated for Laurie Halse Anderson. Now, more than two years after I initially read it, I am feeling Carroll's groove. I wasn't as appreciative as I am now. I think she is one of the truly entertaining horror illustrators out there.<br/><br/>1/29/15 (edited a bit for clarity): This did creep me out. The stories are good and unsettling. I am</span>
  <span id="freeText866138568399863905" style="display:none">11/11/18: I reread this book because I reviewed and shared some of her free short stories here for Halloween, and because I read Speak: The Graphic Novel, which she illustrated for Laurie Halse Anderson. Now, more than two years after I initially read it, I am feeling Carroll's groove. I wasn't as appreciative as I am now. I think she is one of the truly entertaining horror illustrators out there.<br /><br />1/29/15 (edited a bit for clarity): This did creep me out. The stories are good and unsettling. I am rereading Gaiman's The Ocean at the End of the Lane, which is better on many levels, but this is also very good. Initially I thought the kind of wild and splashy art actually undermined the creep-factor in places, it calls attention to itself a little too much, at times? I wasn't sure of her audience, really--is it kids? ya? adults? But when some sort of spaghetti-like material emerges from the dead but animated woman in one of the last stories, I am hooked. I am the audience.<br /><br />I initially got this from the library, because I have way too many books (points to a life of book hoarding), but I have done the rare thing, for me, now, I bought it and am increasingly digging this woman's approach to horror. I think a lot of kids (and adults) will like it, too. I know we all are going to see a lot more of Emily Carroll's work in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="866138568399863905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1925196032?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1925196032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16740202829716309478">I haven't bought books to 'write off'.....but I actually could. In the guest room of of our Airbnb.... I have a book shelf. I like to leave books for our guests to enjoy while they stay with us. We don't offer a TV in the room. We've been getting a lot of return guests ---people who come to town for business-and enjoy staying in our little retreat oasis- private quiet - their own warm pool and sauna. <br/><br/>I've been getting feedback on the books I leave out - so I keep rotating them for repeat 'friend</span>
  <span id="freeText16740202829716309478" style="display:none">I haven't bought books to 'write off'.....but I actually could. In the guest room of of our Airbnb.... I have a book shelf. I like to leave books for our guests to enjoy while they stay with us. We don't offer a TV in the room. We've been getting a lot of return guests ---people who come to town for business-and enjoy staying in our little retreat oasis- private quiet - their own warm pool and sauna. <br /><br />I've been getting feedback on the books I leave out - so I keep rotating them for repeat 'friends'. I bought this graphic book because it can be read in one sitting --it's 'for' adults -'not' children .....and the graphics themselves are sooooo exceptional that even if not all 5 stories are phenomenal.... this book is enjoyable to read and LOOK AT!!!!<br /><br />I liked the first story very much -- called "Our Neighbor's House". It was definitely creepy, not super scary....a little puzzling. I wasn't sure it was believable at all.... but I liked it a lot and the illustrations heightened the story - a perfect match. <br /><br />I liked the other 4 stories - but I liked the illustrations even more. I think there is something in this book for everybody. And if you get out of a hot tub - and are lazy tired -- and simply want to look through a book that captures your attention which is 'gorgeous' to look at and touch..... this book does the trick. <br /><br />Nice guest book --- <br />Taking more suggestions for a few 'guest books' .....I'm all ears!!! <br /><br />Graphic stories with warmth - lovely photos -- I've already got some lovely 'art' books - of women's bodies - aging women - - great colorful yoga books - and so on... looking for new ideas...<br /><br />Looking for more fun reading for guests!!! <br />Note: As the owner of the house - I get to read them too... what else is great????</span>
  <a data-text-id="16740202829716309478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6160091629929009416"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451399343i/17538274._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>If there’s such thing as falling in love at first sight with <i>graphics</i>, I think I just experienced it.</b><br/><br/>No, really. How am I supposed to rate this beautiful set of short stories? I would give it 5 stars solely for the art. The temptation is real, trust me. As it is, I’m going to do some magic average trick and call it a day. Here we go.<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451399343i/17538275._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>No surprise here, of course the art deserves all the stars! If <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3447947.Emily_Carroll' title='Emily Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Emily Carroll</a> uses different techniques in each short story, I can safely say that I loved every one </span>
  <span id="freeText6160091629929009416" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451399343i/17538274._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>If there’s such thing as falling in love at first sight with <i>graphics</i>, I think I just experienced it.</b><br><br>No, really. How am I supposed to rate this beautiful set of short stories? I would give it 5 stars solely for the art. The temptation is real, trust me. As it is, I’m going to do some magic average trick and call it a day. Here we go.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451399343i/17538275._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No surprise here, of course the art deserves all the stars! If <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3447947.Emily_Carroll" title="Emily Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily Carroll</a> uses different techniques in each short story, I can safely say that I loved every one of them. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451401033i/17538410._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>From the colors and brushes to the fonts used to relate her stories, she shows so much talent that I’m let in awe. I want more. I am definitely a fangirl now. This is such a weird feeling for me O_o.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451399343i/17538276._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>See, none of these stories really gave me goosebumps, yet I can’t deny that my heart pounding increased as I was getting closer to each story end… In that aspect, this is a real success. Who needs to be scared to death anyway? Certainly not me. <b>Unsettled, though…</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451401033i/17538411._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451399343i/17538277._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Concerning my involvement and interest in the plots, I have to admit that it was <b>rather uneven</b>. If two of the short stories were definitive 5 stars – <i>the neighbor hat</i> and <i>the nesting place</i> – others let me perplexed, especially because every one of them ended on a cliffhanger, which wasn’t always well-handled in my opinion. While it made me think and created a great shock factor, I was lost sometimes. I mean, perhaps I’m stupid (it <i>is</i> possible) but I didn’t understand everything, to be honest. I must reread it, but really, <i>the lady with cold hands?</i> HUH? Someone explains this ending to me? <br><br><b>Yet I was enthralled from the very first page, which is pretty rare when it comes to graphic novels</b>. Captivating indeed.<br><br><b><u>OVERALL RATING</u> : 4 stars</b><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>

</blockquote></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1362807191" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1362807191?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442465961" href="/book/show/18689586-through-the-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1362807191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9209036877172321349">That wasn't nearly as scary as I was expecting. The art is beautiful though. I love the color palettes she chose for each story; they work very well together. They read like spooky folk tales, and while I wasn't particularly scared by them, they are rather creepy. I felt like a few of the stories ended too abruptly though. I would love for the author to make a longer, single scary story and really expand on what she has here. There wasn't much dialogue either so it goes by really quickly and rel</span>
  <span id="freeText9209036877172321349" style="display:none">That wasn't nearly as scary as I was expecting. The art is beautiful though. I love the color palettes she chose for each story; they work very well together. They read like spooky folk tales, and while I wasn't particularly scared by them, they are rather creepy. I felt like a few of the stories ended too abruptly though. I would love for the author to make a longer, single scary story and really expand on what she has here. There wasn't much dialogue either so it goes by really quickly and relies on the images to deliver the fright. It was fun to read, but not particularly memorable to me. </span>

<div id="review_2161146816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2161146816" />

I thought I wouldn't like it because it's individual short stories, but I was wrong!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3338020918" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3338020918" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3338020918?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3338020918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16937691502559962723">This is a creepy collection of five graphic short stories by Emily Carroll. I think my favorite was “A Lady’s Hands are Cold” out of the five, but all were quite good and equally disturbing. I plan to revisit this hauntingly gorgeous collection again closer to Halloween.<br/><br/>These are like dark fairy tales. If I were to rate this for the illustrations alone, I’d give it five stars. Something I didn’t like was that a few of the endings were abrupt which leaves you drawing your own conclusions.<br/><br/>4****</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1541891378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans">✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780571288656" href="/book/show/23784621-through-the-woods">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of cute kitties, fluffy bunnies and pastel-colored rainbows</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1541891378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12666053307910067524">This one is as <b>darkly beautiful</b> as it is <b>beautifully dark</b>. What more can a nefarious tyrant with a penchant for all things aesthetic ask for, I wonder? Not much, methinks. <b>Not bloody shrimping much</b>.<br/><br/>The <b>graphics and colors</b> are scrumptiously delicious and deliciously scrumptious. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544374920i/26719482._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544374842i/26719477._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Damn</b>, the whole thing is <b>so magnificently done</b> even the <b>fonts</b> are yummy as shrimp. (Which is slightly outrageous, if you ask me.)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544374578i/26719464._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Then there's the <b>Sometimes Creepy Something Spooky Sometimes Serie Stuff</b> (SCS⁵™).<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544375522i/26719504._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There are <b>h</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12666053307910067524" style="display:none">This one is as <b>darkly beautiful</b> as it is <b>beautifully dark</b>. What more can a nefarious tyrant with a penchant for all things aesthetic ask for, I wonder? Not much, methinks. <b>Not bloody shrimping much</b>.<br><br>The <b>graphics and colors</b> are scrumptiously delicious and deliciously scrumptious. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544374920i/26719482._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544374842i/26719477._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Damn</b>, the whole thing is <b>so magnificently done</b> even the <b>fonts</b> are yummy as shrimp. (Which is slightly outrageous, if you ask me.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544374578i/26719464._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then there's the <b>Sometimes Creepy Something Spooky Sometimes Serie Stuff</b> (SCS⁵™).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544375522i/26719504._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are <b>hatchet-wielding damsels</b> in <s>distress</s> lovely yellow dresses.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544375522i/26719505._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And <b>friendly flappers</b> with, errr, problematic <b>dental hygiene</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544376078i/26719600._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then there are <b>Somewhat Shook Up Maidens</b> (SSUM™) who should stay at home and play whist or sew or embroider or some other <b>fascinating occupation</b> of the sort (like any proper, self-respecting, young Regency lady) instead of pretending she can <b>speak to the dead</b> and stuff.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544376874i/26719642._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544376537i/26719633._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Oops</b>.<br><br>(“<b>Serves the silly girl right</b>,” is reported to have said Mrs Bennett when she heard of poor Janna's demise.)<br><br><b>Things</b> go <s>bump</s> <i>
  <b>sshkhhcsshkks</b>
</i> in the night.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544377758i/26719662._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Madame Beauchamp? I wouldn’t bet on it, darling child.</i><br><br>Some puny humans have <b>trouble sleeping</b>. (I’d read Historical Romance, if I were them. Best cure for insomnia, if you ask me.) Either because they did <b>slightly horrible stuff</b> and deserve NOT to succumb to <b>sweet slumber</b> for the rest of the entirety of their entire life…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544377627i/26719659._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>…Or because they are <b>revoltingly innocent little children</b> with super cool, affectionate and <s>not-so-</s>imaginary friends who love to <b>stay up and chat with them</b> at night.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544378706i/26719730._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544378706i/26719729._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>My my, Big Bad, what beautifully, healthy teeth you have! Mind having a word with Ms Flapper of the Dubious Dental Hygiene up there? Pretty sure she’d love to have your dentist’s number and stuff.</i><br><br><b>All in all</b>, I think you could say that all the <b>lovely</b> stories in this collection are <b>heart-warming tales</b> of affection, kindness, good humor, warmth, conviviality and happiness. Ergo, the <b>perfect Christmas gift</b>. QED and stuff.</span>

<div id="review_1292913338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1292913338" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1292913338?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1292913338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16855675000405109790">I’m looking through a window at some trees in the early evening, the trees becoming darker and darker, and I feel something despite myself - the DNA starts moving, remembering a time when the darkness of the trees meant danger. Emily Carroll plays off of those primal fears in the folkish horror stories of Through the Woods, which also warns “It came from the woods. Most strange things do.”<br/><br/>The first story, Our Neighbor’s House, loosely riffs on Red Riding Hood as a trio of sisters are left by the</span>
  <span id="freeText16855675000405109790" style="display:none">I’m looking through a window at some trees in the early evening, the trees becoming darker and darker, and I feel something despite myself - the DNA starts moving, remembering a time when the darkness of the trees meant danger. Emily Carroll plays off of those primal fears in the folkish horror stories of Through the Woods, which also warns “It came from the woods. Most strange things do.”<br /><br />The first story, Our Neighbor’s House, loosely riffs on Red Riding Hood as a trio of sisters are left by their father in their house in the middle of the snow-laden woods. If he doesn’t return in three days, they’re to grab some food and head to their neighbor. He doesn’t return. And a terrifying figure who wears a wide brimmed hat and never stops smiling is waiting outside for the girls…<br /><br />It’s a helluva start to the book which sets a standard that the other stories unfortunately don’t match with each one becoming slightly less inspired than the last. They’re all good stories but none measure up to the chilling brilliance of Our Neighbor’s House. <br /><br />Carroll riffs on the classic fairy tale, Bluebeard, in A Lady’s Hands are Cold, as the new bride of a nobleman hears the haunting cries of a woman throughout the castle at night. The horror is built up really well to a point that feels a bit like the ending of The Shining. <br /><br />His Face All Red begins a theme that’ll last for the next three tales, namely the idea of someone - or something - possessing your body, wearing it like a meat puppet and undergoing a complete personality change (maybe she’s so fearful of this because someone in Carroll’s family had Alzheimer’s?). Two brothers, one a hero, one forgotten, go into the woods to kill the monster terrorising the village - not realising the monsters were never on the outside. <br /><br />My Friend Janna is about two girls who decide to exploit the superstitions of others by pretending to speak to the dead. The Nesting Place is about a girl who goes to her brother’s house in the country and discovers his wife has a terrible secret. It’s MR James crossed with HP Lovecraft! <br /><br />Comics are a unique medium where words and pictures play off each other to tell a story; the great ones have a perfect balance between the two. If I have one criticism of Carroll’s comics - and it really is just one - it’s that the stories feel underwritten with Carroll leaning a bit too much on the imagery to tell the story. Ironically, it ends up making some of the characters feel like the puppets they fear they’ll become rather than rounded, believable characters. <br /><br />Saying that the art is too much of a towering presence in comparison to the writing is a minor critique though that won’t bother many people. That’s because the art is so gorgeous! The final story I haven’t mentioned, In Conclusion, is straight up Red Riding Hood and has some stunning splash pages that look like concept art for the movie Avatar’s alien planet Pandora - using purple to colour trees and rocks at night? What a choice and it really pays off! <br /><br />The blues and yellows of A Lady’s Hands are Cold are made all the more powerful for not being colours you’d associate with a horror story, and the spare use of red against the black and white of Our Neighbor’s House is brilliant. The lines are very confident and the layouts are very imaginative, alternating between panels of varying sizes to free-flowing imagery. <br /><br />The more successful stories - Our Neighbor’s House and His Face All Red - are effective because the horror is less explicit/understandable. It’s almost more threatening to the reader that if you don’t know what the danger is by story’s end, it could happen to you. The less scary stories are conversely the ones that show you the horror straight up which I always find unsatisfying, and that’s the case here. <br /><br />Through the Woods is an excellent collection of fantastical horror stories with a strong fairy-tale theme, almost like a comics adaptation of some of Angela Carter’s stories from The Bloody Chamber. Delightfully creepy reading guaranteed - read them at night in a room with no curtains where the tree branches can cast some interesting shadows in the moonlight… mwahahahaha!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16855675000405109790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540482426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15568098671103867205">Horror stories done stark and right, minimalist and tear-your-face-off creepy.<br/><br/>Seriously. I think I only like one of the five stories, but I loved the other four. Crazy solid scares, and now I've got a good book to read to my daughter once she finally stops needing to sleep with the light on.<br/><br/>After all, we can't have our children growing up unafraid, now can we?<br/><br/>(Puts on a wide brimmed hat and grins in such a way that all of his teeth gleam like piano keys.)<br/><br/>Right?<br/><br/>But my favorite story of all was th</span>
  <span id="freeText15568098671103867205" style="display:none">Horror stories done stark and right, minimalist and tear-your-face-off creepy.<br /><br />Seriously. I think I only like one of the five stories, but I loved the other four. Crazy solid scares, and now I've got a good book to read to my daughter once she finally stops needing to sleep with the light on.<br /><br />After all, we can't have our children growing up unafraid, now can we?<br /><br />(Puts on a wide brimmed hat and grins in such a way that all of his teeth gleam like piano keys.)<br /><br />Right?<br /><br />But my favorite story of all was the one that was told to the monster. How hella cool was that? Totally awesome. :)<br /><br />This is by far the most solid all-around tale(s) of horror I've ever read in a comic. Others might have a lot more creativity, strange plots, more odd characters, but this one excels in doing one thing extremely right:<br /><br />Scaring you.<br /><br />Bravo. :)</span>

<div id="review_1162077139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1162077139" />
    <a title="Sarah Churchill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18321322-sarah-churchill"><img alt="Sarah Churchill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489514919p2/18321322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1162077139?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Churchill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Churchill" href="/user/show/18321322-sarah-churchill">Sarah Churchill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780571288649" href="/book/show/20431035-through-the-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18321322-sarah-churchill?shelf=graphic-novels-and-manga">graphic-novels-and-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18321322-sarah-churchill?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1162077139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5825572696428969702">I'd heard this graphic novel was creepy, but I don't think I'd realised just how creepy. I probably should have guessed when it said it was perfect for fans of Neil Gaiman. <br/><br/>A collection of horror stories that all feature that epitome of childhood creepiness - the woods. The artwork style, simplistic and almost child-like adds to the tension, and Emily Carroll is not afraid of some blood and gore in her illustrations.<br/><br/>This is a definite recommendation for fans of darker graphic novels, horror and </span>
  <span id="freeText5825572696428969702" style="display:none">I'd heard this graphic novel was creepy, but I don't think I'd realised just how creepy. I probably should have guessed when it said it was perfect for fans of Neil Gaiman. <br /><br />A collection of horror stories that all feature that epitome of childhood creepiness - the woods. The artwork style, simplistic and almost child-like adds to the tension, and Emily Carroll is not afraid of some blood and gore in her illustrations.<br /><br />This is a definite recommendation for fans of darker graphic novels, horror and especially for Halloween-time reads. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5825572696428969702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2829515034?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina Haigler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina Haigler" href="/user/show/30268418-tina-haigler">Tina Haigler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30268418-tina-haigler?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2829515034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11438248121442724541">This book is an anthology of horror stories, told in graphic novel form. Horror is my favorite genre, and my favorite medium for it is the graphic novel, so I ended up reading this in one sitting. All the stories found herein had an eerily creepy feel to them, and the artwork matched the tone of it perfectly. The only reason I chose four instead of five stars is because, within the horror world, vague endings are just not my thing. Unhappy endings are perfectly fine, but I'm not a fan of ambiguo</span>
  <span id="freeText11438248121442724541" style="display:none">This book is an anthology of horror stories, told in graphic novel form. Horror is my favorite genre, and my favorite medium for it is the graphic novel, so I ended up reading this in one sitting. All the stories found herein had an eerily creepy feel to them, and the artwork matched the tone of it perfectly. The only reason I chose four instead of five stars is because, within the horror world, vague endings are just not my thing. Unhappy endings are perfectly fine, but I'm not a fan of ambiguous ones. So I do highly recommend this to anyone who loves horror, graphic novels, short stories, unconventional endings, or monster tales. Enjoy!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1369555682" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1369555682" />
    <a title="Mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23106940-mia"><img alt="Mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600049623p2/23106940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1369555682?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mia" href="/user/show/23106940-mia">Mia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=books-with-pictures">books-with-pictures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=wtf-did-i-just-read">wtf-did-i-just-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=great-cover">great-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=best-villains-ever">best-villains-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23106940-mia?shelf=dark-grim-scary">dark-grim-scary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1369555682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11617579301782156297">Some background: I picked up this little beauty at <a href='https://www.drawnandquarterly.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Drawn & Quarterly in Montreal</a>, an amazing bookshop specialising in graphic novels and comics, and when I bought it the cashier told me, "This book is really good." <i>Cool,</i> I thought, <i>that's a good recommendation.</i> But then I read the book and let me tell you that is the understatement of the freaking century.<br/><br/>This book is not just really good. It is fantastic. It is dark and creepy and weird and beautiful and artistic and everything you'd want from </span>
  <span id="freeText11617579301782156297" style="display:none">Some background: I picked up this little beauty at <a href="https://www.drawnandquarterly.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Drawn &amp; Quarterly in Montreal</a>, an amazing bookshop specialising in graphic novels and comics, and when I bought it the cashier told me, "This book is really good." <i>Cool,</i> I thought, <i>that's a good recommendation.</i> But then I read the book and let me tell you that is the understatement of the freaking century.<br><br>This book is not just really good. It is fantastic. It is dark and creepy and weird and beautiful and artistic and everything you'd want from a fairy tale, a horror story, and a graphic novel all rolled into one. And since it is so wonderful and I can't talk about the book as a whole without devolving into rampant, incoherent praise, I'm going to review each of the stories in <i>Through the Woods</i> separately, and in the order they appear. <br><br><br><b>An Introduction</b><br>★★★★★<br><br>While not technically a story, this introduction sets the tone for the rest of the collection. The author, Emily Carroll, talks about how she used to read at night as a child, by the light of a lamp clipped onto her headboard. She imagined that there were things waiting for her in the dark beyond the beam of light, things would grab her and pull her down if she let them. In a way, the rest of the book is about all those things waiting in the darkness.<br><br><br><b>Our Neighbor's House</b><br>★★★★★<br><br>A really strong opening which elicited my first "WHOA". This tale of three sisters, Mary, Beth, and Hannah, in a cold, lonely cabin and what becomes of them is stark, simple, and marvellously scary. It's a feat because we never actually get to see the villain, and we never truly know what becomes of our three sisters, but the ending gives a sense of closure all the same. There's a mounting sense of dread running through the story, culminating in the moment when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the last sister, Beth, wakes up alone in the cabin and knows by the end of the day she will have met her sisters' same fate. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440263224i/15953877._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was also my first immersion into Carroll's artwork, which is stunningly beautiful. Most of her stories take place in the winter, and the dark woods, enormous snow drifts, and tiny cabin are really beautiful imagery for <i>My Neighbor's House</i>. <br><br><br><b>A Lady's Hands are Cold</b><br>★★★★★<br><br><i>"And then it settled into her bones. Every night, that song (that wail) until the girl's insides were clotted with cold heartache."</i><br><br>Many of the stories in this collection read like warped fairy tales, this one especially so. A woman is arranged to marry a rich man and life seems to be going well- she has several handmaids, antique jewellery, fancy gowns, a huge mansion. But every night she hears a strange, keening song emanating from the very house itself, which leads to the dark heart of the story, and the secrets that both her husband and the mansion are hiding. Think Bluebeard, but darker, weirder, and cooler.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440263224i/15953878._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My absolute favourite part about this tale is the last page, when everything finally clicks and you realise, without needing to be told, that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the heroine has been doomed from the very beginning. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Beware, friends- this is one of the gorier stories, as it depicts dismembered limbs and reanimated corpses and such. But it's never overly gory.<br><br><br><b>His Face All Red</b><br>★★★★☆<br><br><i>"But three days later my brother came from the woods. (Most strange things do.) The joy. The joy on all their faces... but it couldn't be him. It couldn't be."</i><br><br>Most strange things come from the woods. Beasts, madmen, and occasionally something...<br><br>...darker.<br><br>This is a pretty open-ended story, not everything is explained, but that's the case with most of the tales in <i>Through the Woods</i>. If you're the type of reader who needs everything to be explained and figured out, then you might be irritated by this book, and especially this story. But if you're like me and you can enjoy a good story without needing to know all of its secrets, you'll love this. Part of the creepiness in this collection emanates from the unknowns in every story, and how one must use one's imagination to fill in the deliberate blanks.<br><br>But, getting back to this one. It's the story of two brothers, a beast, a hole, and what happens in the darkness of the woods when nobody else is around. Plus, Mrs. Carroll has it posted on her website, so you can read it for free <a href="http://emcarroll.com/comics/faceallred/01.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!<br><br><br><b>My Friend Janna</b><br>★★★☆☆<br><br><i>"I admit, at the time, we thought it a splendid diversion. Because I was what waited within the walls of Janna's mother's house. No ghosts, no spirits. No demons. 'Are you there, O visitors? O otherworldly things, O creatures of the faraway darkness!'<br><br>Me, who would scratch and kick when I heard my cue. Me, who would shake the plates from the wall."</i><br><br>While I really liked the premise- two friends, Janna and Yvonne, who trick their neighbours into thinking that Janna can speak to the dead- I wasn't crazy about the execution. I was never really sure why, or how, or by what <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Janna became haunted. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And while I loved reading Janna's nonsensical notes, I wish they were explained more than just "Oh well Janna's gone bonkers look at this stupid stuff she's written".<br><br><br><b>The Nesting Place</b><br>★★★☆☆<br><br>Mabel, nicknamed Bell, spends summer vacation at her older brother's house, ringed by ominous woods she's been warned to stay out of and an unsettling feeling from the cook, Madame Beauchamp, and Bell's brother's mysteriously cheery wife, Rebecca.<br><br>This story is remarkable because it reads a lot like a book condensed into a few pages. It has a great plot, characters with backstories, mysteries, twists, and, in keeping with the theme, monsters. In fact, I loved the monsters in this one, because I've always been a fan of monsters that burrow deep within you and whom you don't realise are there until it's too late. They're the scariest kind, in my opinion, and they're the ones that grace the freakish pages of <i>The Nesting Place</i>. <br><br>So why only three stars, then? Well... I just didn't get it. It felt like it had been building up to a bigger reveal then the typical <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[skin-wearing monsters and red worms protruding out of Rebecca's face. I also didn't understand the significance of the crooked teeth- what does that have to do with the skin-worm things? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This is definitely the goriest story, though, so be warned. There's some pretty startling imagery, such as: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440263224i/15953879._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Yeah. Ick.<br><br><br><b>In Conclusion</b><br>★★★★★<br><br>A really, really wonderful and short conclusion in the vein of Little Red Riding Hood, which closes up the collection with this amazing quote: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409625432i/11001026._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>On this book as a whole, I have to agree with J. Caleb Mozzocco, who wrote in <a href="http://robot6.comicbookresources.com/2014/08/anxiously-ever-after-emily-carrolls-through-the-woods/" rel="nofollow noopener">his review</a> that, "<i>Through the Woods</i> is thus a completely 21st-century form used to tell new stories that read as if they could have been centuries old." And while I would love to say that this hauntingly beautiful collection is perfect for Halloween, I would really recommend reading it in the cold of winter, when the darkness of the woods and the things that wait within can truly come to life.<br><br><br><br>P.S. Also! Emily Carroll has a bunch of other cool stuff on her website, my favourite being an interactive comic/story called <a href="http://emcarroll.com/comics/margot/" rel="nofollow noopener">Margot's Room</a><br><br>P.P.S. This book pairs incredibly well with the song <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sDaGSJpGMmA" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Woods Somewhere</a> by Hozier. They are perfect together.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11617579301782156297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1041253427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1041253427" />
    <a title="Hershey " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19468761-hershey"><img alt="Hershey " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599546236p2/19468761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1041253427?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hershey " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hershey " href="/user/show/19468761-hershey">Hershey </a>
      </span>

        rated it

Shucks. I hoped at the end of each story that the next one was going to scare the shit out of me but the only story that kind of freaked me out a little was The Nesting Place. <br><br>However, I really enjoyed every single story and the illustrations were extremely gorgeous! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421480706i/13381278._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18279314672633889825"><b>What a beautiful book! The illustrations are simply amazing.</b><br/><br/>In september, when summer is ending, I always feel like reading spooky stories. This book didn't disappoint!<br/><br/>The short stories were interesting and creepy. Unfortunately, I wasn't really satisfied with most endings, but that didn't stop me from enjoying my read. <br/><br/>...and I have to repeat: <b>this book is a work or art!</b><br/><br/><i>5*: Sad to finish it, this book was amazing<br/>4*: Really liked it!<br/>3*: Liked it<br/>2*: Fell asleep a couple of times during my reading</i></span>
  <span id="freeText18279314672633889825" style="display:none"><b>What a beautiful book! The illustrations are simply amazing.</b><br /><br />In september, when summer is ending, I always feel like reading spooky stories. This book didn't disappoint!<br /><br />The short stories were interesting and creepy. Unfortunately, I wasn't really satisfied with most endings, but that didn't stop me from enjoying my read. <br /><br />...and I have to repeat: <b>this book is a work or art!</b><br /><br /><i>5*: Sad to finish it, this book was amazing<br />4*: Really liked it!<br />3*: Liked it<br />2*: Fell asleep a couple of times during my reading... but not entirely boring!<br />1*: Why did I bother to finish it?!</i></span>

    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MWGtqCCGx1V8UIlWdm03Vej/9FsLmf6WHMDOHMYJ9V6RcoTFlGgW9y1Evo6nPRWdodKQYDc9VESkstCW/aQ6Jg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RwZ5muVMsqFRLFeBpR3zJa3MpNTWE5efQ6XnysVBN5jnFVD3UaJjAwA4YFl0TdHt5OHA7+q3PU371/lA/uz44A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer13207051921863996280">My name is Emily Carroll, and I was born in June of 1983. I grew up in London (Ontario) but moved to Vancouver for work after graduating Sheridan College's Classical Animation program. I have since moved back to Ontario, and now live in Stratford with my wife, Kate Craig. We have a very large cat.<br/><br/>Source: <a href='http://www.emcarroll.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>About Emily</a>.</span>
